    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer69448936847194535">The year is 1881. Meet the Mackenzie family—rich, powerful, dangerous, eccentric. A lady couldn't be seen with them without ruin. Rumors surround them—of tragic violence, of their mistresses, of their dark appetites, of scandals that set England and Scotland abuzz. <br/> <br/>The youngest brother, Ian, known as the Mad Mackenzie, spent most of his young life in an asylum, and everyo</span>
  <span id="freeText69448936847194535" style="display:none">The year is 1881. Meet the Mackenzie family—rich, powerful, dangerous, eccentric. A lady couldn't be seen with them without ruin. Rumors surround them—of tragic violence, of their mistresses, of their dark appetites, of scandals that set England and Scotland abuzz. <br /> <br />The youngest brother, Ian, known as the Mad Mackenzie, spent most of his young life in an asylum, and everyone agrees he is decidedly odd. He's also hard and handsome and has a penchant for Ming pottery and beautiful women. <br /> <br />Beth Ackerley, widow, has recently come into a fortune. She has decided that she wants no more drama in her life. She was raised in drama—an alcoholic father who drove them into the workhouse, a frail mother she had to nurse until her death, a fussy old lady she became constant companion to. No, she wants to take her money and find peace, to travel, to learn art, to sit back and fondly remember her brief but happy marriage to her late husband. <br /> <br />And then Ian Mackenzie decides he wants her. <br /> <br />The first of a new historical series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="69448936847194535" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Yes, Ian Mackenzie has Asbergers Syndrome. I could never say that in the book, because there wasn't a term for it at the time the novel is set (1880s)<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Yes, Ian Mackenzie has Asbergers Syndrome. I could never say that in the book, because there wasn't a term for it at the time the novel is set (1880s).<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<div id="review_1267141603" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1267141603" />
    <a title="Jessica&#39;s Totally Over The Top Book Obsession" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28967089-jessica-s-totally-over-the-top-book-obsession"><img alt="Jessica&#39;s Totally Over The Top Book Obsession" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1511556834p2/28967089.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1267141603?book_show_action=true">Apr 29, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica&#39;s Totally Over The Top Book Obsession" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica&#39;s Totally Over The Top Book Obsession" href="/user/show/28967089-jessica-s-totally-over-the-top-book-obsession">Jessica&#39;s Totally Over The Top Book Obsession</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1267141603" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3941464570328825176"><b>5 Crazy in love Stars </b><br/><br/><a href='http://s327.photobucket.com/user/jessica_hatfield1/media/715508_zpsutdhsk3p.gif.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1430634855ra/14737237.gif' alt=' photo 715508_zpsutdhsk3p.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>First read May 2nd 2015 <br/>Reread 8/14/2016 <br/>Re reread 6/24/2017<br/>Re re reread lol July 18th 2020<br/><br/>*I love that no matter what mood I'm in or how many times I read this book I can pick it up and get lost in a beautiful love story!*<br/><br/><b>*Spoilers*</b><br/><br/><b>“When I saw you, I knew I had to take you away from him. He had no idea what you were worth, just like he can’t price the damn bowls. He’s a philistine.”</b><br/><br/>Let me just say that with Historical Romances I either love em or I hate em. I loved thi</span>
  <span id="freeText3941464570328825176" style="display:none"><b>5 Crazy in love Stars </b><br><br><a href="http://s327.photobucket.com/user/jessica_hatfield1/media/715508_zpsutdhsk3p.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1430634855ra/14737237.gif" alt=" photo 715508_zpsutdhsk3p.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>First read May 2nd 2015 <br>Reread 8/14/2016 <br>Re reread 6/24/2017<br>Re re reread lol July 18th 2020<br><br>*I love that no matter what mood I'm in or how many times I read this book I can pick it up and get lost in a beautiful love story!*<br><br><b>*Spoilers*</b><br><br><b>“When I saw you, I knew I had to take you away from him. He had no idea what you were worth, just like he can’t price the damn bowls. He’s a philistine.”</b><br><br>Let me just say that with Historical Romances I either love em or I hate em. I loved this one so much! OMG it was so different and freaking awesome that I couldn't put it down. Hell I didn't even want to stop long enough to write this review. I wanted to just move on to the next book in this series... This was such a beautiful and heartwarming story about Two flawed people finding happiness with each other just the way they are!<br><br><b>“It’s part of the very intriguing package that is Ian Mackenzie.”</b><br><br><br><b> What this book is about </b><br><br>Beth Ackerley is a widow who just inherited enough money to be set for life. Engaged to a man she thinks is respectable, Beth is ready to start a drama free life and to find a little bit of happiness since the loss of her beloved first husband. Everything changes when she meets Lord Ian Mackenzie at the opera. While shaking her hand he slips a note into her glove. When she reads it, it tells her that her soon to be husband has women on the side and has a slave fetish. Upset by the news she flees the Opera to get fresh air, where Ian grabs her and asks her to marry him instead! She knows what everyone says about Lord Ian Mackenzie (that he is crazy), but she feels drawn to him. Then he kisses her and she doesn't care if he is crazy she just wants more! What is a respectable woman to do? Run for her life or take her chances with Mad Mackenzie.<br><br><br><b>“Belong to me.” “No one here to dispute that at the moment.” “Always mine. Always, Beth.”</b><br><br><br>Ian:<br><br><a href="http://s327.photobucket.com/user/jessica_hatfield1/media/Ian_zpsdezlekos.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1430634402i/14737070.jpg" alt=" photo Ian_zpsdezlekos.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br><b>“Is this what love feels like?” he whispered to her. “I don’t like it, my Beth. It hurts too much.”</b><br><br>Ian stole my heart. He is one of the most endearing and memorable characters I have read in a long time. Ian is considered mad. It is obvious that Ian has Asperger's Syndrome, of course back then they didn't know what any of that is so he was labeled mad, beat , tossed in an asylum to be tortured with electric shock therapy and, beat some more until his father dies and his brother the Duke gets him released. Ian believes he can't love and he doesn't understand others emotions, he also has a lot of pint up rage, but Ian is a fighter. A overcomer that knows he doesn't fit in, but makes a life for himself anyways. I love him with Beth how hard he tries to understand what she is feeling, trying hard to look her in the eyes and he even tries to make a joke or two. He was a pure and in-depth Character that you can never forget!<br><br><br><b>“We don’t fit in, you and me,” he said. “We’re both oddities no one knows what to do with. But we fit together.” He took her hand, pressed her palm to his, then laced their fingers through each other’s. “We fit.”<br><br><br>“Your being with me makes it stop. It’s like the Ming bowls—when I touch them and feel them, everything stops. Nothing matters. You are the same. That is why I brought you here, to keep you with me, where you can please make . .. everything . . . stop.”<br><br><br>“For God’s sake.” Ian spun away, unable to stand still. “I’m not your Thomas, your vicar. I never will be. I know you’ll never look at me the way you looked at him.” She stared at him, white-faced. “What do you mean?” He turned back. “You look at me like I’m the Mad Mackenzie. It’s in the back of your mind all the time.” He tapped the side of her head. “You can never forget about my madness, and you pity me for it.”</b><br><br><br>Beth:<br><br><b>“I am a wicked, wicked woman,” she murmured. “Kiss me again.”</b><br><br><a href="http://s327.photobucket.com/user/jessica_hatfield1/media/beth_zpsi4d97mbo.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1430634402i/14737071._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo beth_zpsi4d97mbo.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Beth is perfect for Ian. She is sweet and loving. She is also strong willed and stands up for Ian and what she believes in. She is very outspoken and said what is on her mind! She's had a hard life which gives her courage and a backbone, but it makes her not fit in so well in social settings. I loved how Beth loved and accepted Ian just the way he is not trying to fix or change him. She makes him laugh, smile and she believes in him. She also really wants Ian and is not shy about it. <br><br><br><b>“Explain to me what loving feels like, Beth. I want to understand.” “The love for another’s body. But also love for their heart and their mind, and for all the silly things they do, no matter how absurd. Your world brightens when they walk into a room, dims when they leave it again. You want to be with the beloved so you can see him and touch him and hear his voice, but you want his happiness as well. It’s selfish, but not entirely so.”<br><br><br>“I am Ian’s wife because I choose to be,” she said. “Whether we live in a grand mansion or a tiny boardinghouse, it makes no difference.”<br><br><br>“I like it,” she said. “I love how hard your staff is, yet the skin is silken. I remember how it feels under my tongue.”<br><br><br>“I’m the Mad Mackenzie.” Beth pressed his face between her hands, anger suddenly rising. “That is other people’s explanation, because they don’t understand you.”</b><br><br><a href="http://s327.photobucket.com/user/jessica_hatfield1/media/7d34475ba2730afd7c49a7585db57e2e_zps0q2fasd5.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1430634402i/14737072.jpg" alt=" photo 7d34475ba2730afd7c49a7585db57e2e_zps0q2fasd5.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br><b>“Never mind. You are a rogue and a scoundrel, and I love every single second of it.”</b><br><br>Beth and Ian are a sweet couple and you could feel the strong connection they have like they are real people. They have some steamy chemistry and both really enjoy carnal relations. The other Mackenzie brothers are loud, rude , manly and totally lovable. This story touched me deeply. I have a niece with autism so reading a book where pure love overcomes differences and difficulties to live happily ever after gives me hope that someday she will get hers too. <br><br><b>“My Beth,” he whispered, his breath hot on her swollen lips. “Thank you.” “For what?” Beth couldn’t stop crying, but she smiled, her face aching with it. “Setting me free.”</b><br><br><a href="http://s327.photobucket.com/user/jessica_hatfield1/media/c08db86d22f4b92328618180d387feb2_zpsdiyt2agm.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1430634402i/14737073.jpg" alt=" photo c08db86d22f4b92328618180d387feb2_zpsdiyt2agm.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I can't wait to read the others. Below I leave my favorite moment in the book:<br><br><b>“I love you,” he said. Beth caught her breath, and sudden tears blurred her vision. “Love you,” Ian repeated. His gaze bore into hers harder than Hart’s ever could hope to. “Love you, love you, love you, love you, love you love you love you...” “Ian.” Beth laughed. “Love you,” he murmured against her lips, her face, against the curve of her neck. “Love you.” “I love you, too. Are you going to say it all night?” “I’ll say it until I’m in you so hard I can’t speak.” “I suppose I’ll have to put up with that. It might be difficult, though I wouldn’t mind finding out.” He paused. “Are you joking?” Beth laughed until she slid out of the seat, but when she landed on the floor, Ian was right beside her. “Yes. I was joking.” She caught lan’s lapels in her hands. “I believe carnality is definitely called for. Perhaps we should send for Curry to pull out the bed.”</b><br><br><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://jessicasoverthetopbookobsession.blogspot.com/">http://jessicasoverthetopbookobsessio...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3941464570328825176" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><br><b>This is one of the best books I've read. <a href="http://beta.photobucket.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380374026ra/727924.gif" alt=" photo 279453.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br>This is one of the best historicals I've read. <a href="http://beta.photobucket.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380374026ra/727924.gif" alt=" photo 279453.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br>This book has one of the best heroes I've ever read. <a href="http://beta.photobucket.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380374026ra/727924.gif" alt=" photo 279453.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br>This book has one of the best heroines I've read. <a href="http://beta.photobucket.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380374026ra/727924.gif" alt=" photo 279453.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br>This book has a fantastic story. <a href="http://beta.photobucket.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380374026ra/727924.gif" alt=" photo 279453.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br>This book has made me love two women. <a href="http://beta.photobucket.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380374026ra/727924.gif" alt=" photo 279453.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br>This book made me love four men. <a href="http://beta.photobucket.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380374026ra/727924.gif" alt=" photo 279453.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br>This book made me want to read five books at the same time. <a href="http://beta.photobucket.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380374026ra/727924.gif" alt=" photo 279453.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br><br><br>This book is in my heart and it will never go out. <a href="http://beta.photobucket.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/529986.gif" alt=" photo 836920.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a> </b><br><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Your being with me makes it stop. It’s like the Ming bowls—when I touch them and feel them, everything stops. Nothing matters. You are the same. That is why I brought you here, to keep you with me, where you can please make ... everything <br>... stop.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br><br><br><b>The story</b><br><br>Ian decides to save a widow from an unfortunate marriage, and ends up proposing to her in the same evening. She is something fascinating to him, and he wants to have her.<br>The widow is Beth, who recently became an heiress, and is extremely attracted to Ian. Still, she declines and goes to Paris. Ian, of course, follows her :D<br>In Paris, Beth meets Ian's brother Mac and his wife Isabella, who are separated. Isabella takes Beth under her wing and decides to do a bit of matchmaking :D<br>At the same time, a detective is investigating a murder that leads to Ian, and he does everything he can to prove it.<br>Beth can't stop thinking about Ian, and after some time, she proposes they have an affair. She knows he can't fall in love with her, but can she keep herself from falling in love with him?<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“I am incapable of love. I will not offer it to you.” <br>Beth wondered what was more heartbreaking, the words themselves or the flat tone of voice with which he delivered them.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>Now, these are just the happenings in the book. The REAL story is Ian. How everyone sees him, how he sees himself, his terrible past, and his love affair with Beth. <br>I can't say how much I loved it. Ian changes so much through the book, it's amazing! <br>I loved the rest of the story too, the murder mistery was interesting and I couldn't guess who did it until the end, although I had my suspicions on who DIDN'T do it pretty early :D<br>This was a slow build, introduction to a lot of characters that will have their own books, and it was done SO WELL that I wanted to start those books while I was reading this one! I seriously can't wait to read them all, I know I won't stop until I finish this series.<br>The writing style is GREAT, easy to read, although I noticed some modern expressions. <br>The sex was hot, even though one scene (and that is my only objection with the book) did seem weird for a historical, as in, the first I've read where the heroine does a <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[blow job, and she swallows.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> It wouldn't be that weird if it was an experienced widow in question, but she's never done it, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[and she wants to swallow? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Anyway it may have been hotter if it wasn't described by her writing it down in her diary. Seriously not hot.<br>About the modern expressions, I think Ian at one point said that "she went down on him" :D I really don't think they said that back then :D Maybe I'm wrong, but I don't know...<br>But ok, like I said, my only objection, everything else in the book was fabulous and I absolutely loved it &lt;3<br><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“You make no sense, my lord. If you don’t care about my fortune or whether I love you, why on earth do you wish to marry me?”<br>Ian reached for the curl again as though he couldn’t stop himself. “Because I want to bed you.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380374026i/727925.jpg" alt="Image Hosted by ImageShack.us" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>He’d marry her for a very basic reason: to have her with him every night, every day, every afternoon, and every time in between. He walked down the boulevard, something in him awakening and breaking free.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br><br><br><b>The characters</b><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380374026i/727926.jpg" alt="Image Hosted by ImageShack.us" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Beth’s fragile trust was in Ian’s hands. He’d growled that he didn’t want to be protected, but the instinct to protect her was strong. Beth was so alone in the world, so vulnerable, and she didn’t even realize it.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br><b>Ian</b><br><br>Everyone thinks he's mad. His father put him in an asylum when he was just a boy, where he went through hell. After his father's death, his brother Hart set him free, and it took him a long while to adjust. <br>I won't tell you more because it's just heartbreaking and you'll feel it more when you read it for yourself. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“What was it like?” His words were so low she barely caught them. “Explain to me what loving feels like, Beth. I want to understand.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>Ian has a light form of autism. He doesn't look anyone in the eye, and has some OCDs. He isn't able to read people's faces, recognise their emotions, he basically has to be told what they're thinking.<br>He has some form of photographic memory, he's a genious. He remembers every conversation and everything he's ever read, is good with numbers, but bad with people. He gets fascinated by simple things and ignores everything else.<br>He is just such a complex and incredibly written character! <br>I couldn't NOT feel for him, and I couldn't NOT adore him! Especially because he began to change gradually through the book, all of it thanks to Beth. Even though he said he isn't capable of love, I think he fell in love with Beth pretty early, but just didn't understand it.<br>The more it went, the more we found out about his past, and I can believe the asylum made him worse, gave him more fears, and made him shut down more. Being with Beth set him free, made him laugh, made him wish to spend more time with her, instead of being alone. It was just beautiful to watch him change, and my heart went out to him every step of the way. And when he looked her in the eyes <a href="http://beta.photobucket.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380374026ra/727927.gif" alt=" photo 815594.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>Ian is definitely one of the most complex characters I've read, and I just love him to pieces! <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"Ian’s life was dictated by other people—events and conversations swirled past him before he could follow them; other people decided whether he’d live in an asylum or out of it, whether he’d go to Rome or wait in London. Events flowed and ebbed, and as long as they didn’t interfere with his interests, like finding elusive Ming pottery, he let them happen.<br>Now Beth had landed in the swift stream of his life, and she’d stuck there like a rock.<br>Everything else swirled past him, but like an anchor, Beth stayed."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380374026i/727928.png" alt="Image Hosted by ImageShack.us" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"I do not think of him as Lord Ian Mackenzie, aristocratic brother of a duke and well beyond my reach; not as the Mad Mackenzie, an eccentric people stare at and whisper about.<br>To me, he is simply Ian."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br><b>Beth</b><br><br>She's a widow, recently became rich, and recently became fiancéless due to the divine intervention of Lord Ian Mackenzie.<br>After nine years of being alone, she wants company, wants to feel desire again, and it happens every time she's near Ian. <br>She doesn't see him as a madman, she knows he's different, but not crazy. <br>After they begin their affair, she begins to fall in love with him, knowing he can't love her back.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"Ian cannot do something so simple as hold a woman’s hand. He moves his thumb up my wrist and under my glove, finding points that shoot wild heat through my body. He caresses the inside of my palm with soft fingers, and then he threads his fingers through mine and holds hard, as though teaching me that my hand belongs there with his."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>Beth is a fantastic heroine! She is so understanding, and smart! She has courage and doesn't let people walk all over her. <br>I just loved the way she didn't judge anyone, especially Ian. She doesn't jump to conclusions, and asks Ian to tell her everything (instead of all those heroines that hear something, get mortally wounded in the heart for the hero deceiving them and they run away to another city or something until they get together again). Nope, nothing like that here. Ian and Beth had a very mature relationship, even though Ian refrained in telling her anything about the murders, but she managed to find that out for herself :D<br>She stood up to the inspector, and to Hart when he was overprotective, and damn I could just go on and on :DDDD Love her! The end!<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Beth fixed him with an icy stare. “Rest assured, I am not prone to swooning. I might have the footmen throw you out, yes, but swoon, no.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br><br><br><b>The rest of the Mackenzie family</b><br><br>I love them already!!!! It isn't normal, but I guess the author did an excellent job with the introductions, they wormed their way inside my brain and I won't be still until I've read all the books that are published!!!!<br>Isabella, I love her too! I feel very sorry for her because I know she still loves Mac, and I desperately want to know what happened between them!!!!!<br>Cameron and his son are interesting as well, can't wait too read his story too. I wonder what happened with his wife and all. Sounds terrible! And I wonder who his love interest will be :D can't wait!<br>Hart.... Wow that guy is intense! I think the first BDSM hero in a historical!!! Well, at least what I could gather, it was something like that :D The guy is into some kinky stuff!!!! There was mentioned a lady that ditched him, can't remember her name, but I bet she'll be in his book :DDDD Can't wait for that one too!!!<br><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“All of us are mad in some way,” Ian said. “I have a memory that won’t let go of details.<br>Hart is obsessed with politics and money. Cameron is a genius with horses, and Mac paints like a god. ...<br>We all have our madness.<br>Mine is just the most obvious.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380374026i/727929.jpg" alt="Image Hosted by ImageShack.us" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><br><br><b>I don't know what else to say about this book except - READ IT!!!<br><br>I recommend it to every historical fan, and to those of you who are not! <br><br>It's that good, and it's that much worth reading!<br><br>Amazing.</b><br><br><br><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/79447060?book_show_action=true">Nov 30, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="UniquelyMoi ~ BlithelyBookish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="UniquelyMoi ~ BlithelyBookish" href="/user/show/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish">UniquelyMoi ~ BlithelyBookish</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Historical Romance Lovers - Anyone who loves a hero who needs &quot;fixing&quot;</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=2010-reads">2010-reads</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=author-jennifer-ashley">author-jennifer-ashley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=illness-mental">illness-mental</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=reviewed-by-me">reviewed-by-me</a>,

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer79447060" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7129788841531889692"><br/><b>Edited to add a note from the author which can be found at the end of this review.</b><br/><br/><i>Review contains minor spoilers</i><br/><br/>This is my first read of any of Jennifer Ashley’s works and I was not disappointed, in fact, I was very, very pleased. I found her writing style to be flowing and well thought out, and her ability to weave a tale that kept me wondering, *sighing* and hopeful through the entire novel made this, for me, a story that was “un-put-downable” (Yep, I made up that word. ) *grins* <br/><br/>This is one o</span>
  <span id="freeText7129788841531889692" style="display:none"><br /><b>Edited to add a note from the author which can be found at the end of this review.</b><br /><br /><i>Review contains minor spoilers</i><br /><br />This is my first read of any of Jennifer Ashley’s works and I was not disappointed, in fact, I was very, very pleased. I found her writing style to be flowing and well thought out, and her ability to weave a tale that kept me wondering, *sighing* and hopeful through the entire novel made this, for me, a story that was “un-put-downable” (Yep, I made up that word. ) *grins* <br /><br />This is one of those times that, even though much of the story is based on Ian’s past, we didn’t need to have it all laid out in a prologue. Instead, we learn through flashbacks told from his brothers’ points of view, as well as Ian’s, about the youngest Mackenzie being institutionalized and subjected to all manner of horrible experiments performed under the guise of "treatments." Jennifer Ashley did an excellent job of giving us just enough details of his dismal existence for us to really understand what Ian had been subjected to, without going into so much detail as to make this an uncomfortable read. <br /><br />From what I understand from reading other reviews, Ian’s “madness” is a form of autism, Aperger's Syndrome, though I don’t remember anywhere in the book where they gave it any specific medical name, not even one accepted during the time of this story. “Madness” is such an all encompassing word, but I suppose with the way the characteristics of his condition manifested themselves, “madness” would have summed it all up quite well. <br /><br />I loved that we were introduced to Ian right away, and got a glimpse of one of his “quirks” – his passion for Ming vases – early on. A man of complex contradictions, Ian is often withdrawn, yet easily enraged. He has a childlike honesty about him – he literally doesn’t know how to lie – yet understands that he can avoid telling the truth by withholding it. If I were a licensed psychiatrist/psychologist, I would likely still be on page 1 trying to unravel the complex and intricate weave that makes Ian, Ian – a hero unlike any other hero I have ever read about, and I can’t tell you how refreshing that is.<br /><br />Beth, a compassionate, nurturing woman unconcerned with society’s ideas of propriety and morals spent most of her life giving service to those in need. She had <i>cared</i> for her alcoholic mother until she passed, then as the wife of Thomas, the vicar, she <i>cared</i> for those in his flock. When, after only a year of marriage he became ill, Beth <i>cared</i> for him until he passed. She was fortunate enough to then become the companion of an wealthy, opinionated old woman with whom she spent many years, and when the woman became ill, Beth <i>cared</i> for her, too, until she died. <i>Care, care, care</i>…caring for people who were unable do so for themselves was something Beth was all too familiar with. Only a person who had walked in Beth’s shoes could see past the rumors and the lies which shroud the Mackenzie family. She was able to peel away the layers and see that there was much more to them than they allowed people to see. It took very little time for her to realize how much Ian needed her, but knowing what I did about Ian, I had expected that this would turn out to be a story of unrequited love. I believed that Beth would care for him, maybe even grow to love him, in spite of his madness – or perhaps because of it – yet never feel his love in return. Nor would she expect it because he had made it clear to her that he couldn’t… literally <i>could not</i>, love her.<br /><br />I found it interesting that Ian believed he couldn’t feel a person’s love for him, nor could he return that love and yet, he felt and reacted to fear, anger, disgust, compassion, lust… so this didn’t make a lot of sense to me. When he first met Beth, he had to have felt something for her or he wouldn’t have been compelled to help her. As the story progressed and situations came about, he reacted much the way a man in love would; he became protective, possessive, domineering and demanding. So, I found myself thinking that perhaps because he had never felt this kind of love for someone, he didn’t know what to label these new emotions, or how to express them. Thankfully this issue was resolved to my satisfaction towards the end of the book.<br /><br />I would love to go on and on, dissecting each little nuance of both Ian and Beth, but there are so many *sigh* moments and subtle things to love about them both that it would take pages and pages - and honestly, I don’t want to deprive you of finding them yourself because it’s those moments that make this, for me, a truly great story.<br /><br />Ian’s 3 brothers, Hart, Mac and Cameron, played big parts in this book and their characters, as well as their checkered pasts, were so well developed that I am already impatiently awaiting their stories.<br /><br />While The Madness of Lord Ian Mackenzie is not exactly what I had anticipated, it turned out to be more than I had hoped for. By page 5 I was completely captivated by Ian and by page 13, I wanted to bring him home with me and love him forever. *sigh* But I will have to be content in knowing that he has his Beth to love him like no one else ever could.<br /><br />Note: For my friends who I know are concerned about the sexuality of the book - having read some reviews calling this erotica - while I would say that the “heat index” on this is pretty high, the sex itself could be considered pretty mainstream - no menage, no anal. (Hope this helps)<br /><br /><b>Update:</b> There have been many discussion about Ian's "madness," and what it is exactly. I sent Ms. Ashley an email today and asked her if she would share with us some insight into writing Ian, his "madness," and her research. I was thrilled to have gotten an answer right away and with her permission, I'm posting her reply:<br /><br />"Ian has Asperger's (which, as you say, is high-functioning autism). I wanted to explore what it would be like to have Asperger's before it or autism was recognized or even had a name.<br /> <br />People with Asperger's can have a variety of traits, and not every person has the same (e.g., some are fine with looking into other people's eyes, some have a great sense of humor, while others are painfully shy and take everything literally). So Ian has Asperger's and a little OCD (obsessive-compulsive disorder). A great memory for certain things, usually very focused on details.<br /> <br />I did a ton of research on Asperger's and autism (heartbreaking stuff), and then started writing. Once I was writing, though, I totally fell in love with Ian! He was the toughest hero I've ever written, but he was worth the pain. :-)<br /><br />Jennifer Ashley"<br /><br />My sincere thanks to Ms. Ashley for sharing that information with us, and for giving us Ian, a truly *sigh* worthy hero.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7129788841531889692" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_55434213" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/55434213" />
    <a title="Dina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1918270-dina"><img alt="Dina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1460302951p2/1918270.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/55434213?book_show_action=true">May 08, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dina" href="/user/show/1918270-dina">Dina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1918270-dina?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer55434213" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11980567139732795669">Almost everyone who's read this book loved it to pieces, so my expectations were pretty high when I started it. High expectations can be a blessing... or a curse. Now that I finished this read, I can't help wondering what is "wrong" with me because, I'm sorry to say, I don't understand what all the fuss is about.<br/><br/>I liked Ms. Ashley's writing - this was my 1st book by her - and I thought the premise - the hero is "mad" - was interesting and unique, but the <i>romance</i> didn't work for me. <i>Lust</i> was very</span>
  <span id="freeText11980567139732795669" style="display:none">Almost everyone who's read this book loved it to pieces, so my expectations were pretty high when I started it. High expectations can be a blessing... or a curse. Now that I finished this read, I can't help wondering what is "wrong" with me because, I'm sorry to say, I don't understand what all the fuss is about.<br /><br />I liked Ms. Ashley's writing - this was my 1st book by her - and I thought the premise - the hero is "mad" - was interesting and unique, but the <i>romance</i> didn't work for me. <i>Lust</i> was very well depicted and the sex scenes were steamy hot, but <i>love</i> was nowhere in sight, IMHO. How can you fall in love with someone you only meet between the sheets? Ian and Beth had barely exchanged a few <i>conversations</i> before they found themselves <i>in love</i> with each other, and that pattern didn't change after they got married. I had a hard time buying their love - especially because I was constantly reminded that Ian didn't <i>understand</i> what Beth said half the time. He became completely <s>obsessed</s> devoted to her from the moment they met and I can go along with that - hey, I <i>have</i> bought that scenario in several books before and I <i>will</i> keep doing that, no doubt about it - but I need to feel that special connection between the H/h. Sadly, I didn't feel that with Ian and Beth.<br /><br />Halfway through the book, the story took a turn and the romance was left aside to give space to a convoluted murder mystery. I won't go into details here because I don't want to give any spoilers away, but the "investigation" conducted by Beth was silly. I can't understand how she just solved something that Hart (Ian's older brother) and the Scotland Yard itself had failed for 5 years! Super Woman, thy name is Beth.<br /><br />That 2nd half of the story annoyed me and made me drop my rating to 3 stars. I still needed Ian and Beth to convince me they were in love, but I had to content myself with pages and pages of Beth digging into the Mackenzies' past and working on solving the murder mystery.<br /><br />Another "problem" I had with this book is, it screamed "First Book in the Series". Ian's brothers - all future heroes in the series, I'm sure - and their problems were featured in detail, taking my attention away from Ian and Beth.<br /><br />All in all, this wasn't an altogether bad read to me. I really enjoyed the 1st half of the story, when Ms. Ashely was still developing Ian and Beth's relationship. But then, wham! They were in love and I didn't know how that had happened. Oh well...<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11980567139732795669" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_615387807" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/615387807" />
    <a title="Navessa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18104163-navessa"><img alt="Navessa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1444162983p2/18104163.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/615387807?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Navessa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Navessa" href="/user/show/18104163-navessa">Navessa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18104163-navessa?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18104163-navessa?shelf=insufferable-mc">insufferable-mc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18104163-navessa?shelf=highlanders">highlanders</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18104163-navessa?shelf=mental-health">mental-health</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18104163-navessa?shelf=drama-drama-drama">drama-drama-drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18104163-navessa?shelf=normalized-sexism">normalized-sexism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18104163-navessa?shelf=books-everyone-loves-but-i-hate">books-everyone-loves-but-i-hate</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18104163-navessa?shelf=not-a-friend-of-feminism">not-a-friend-of-feminism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18104163-navessa?shelf=divisive-characters">divisive-characters</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer615387807" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13121676186899418438"><b>2.5 stars</b><br/><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[I’m rounding up to prove that I’m not a complete asshole all the time. <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br/><br/>So, first things first. The male lead in this book, Lord Ian MacKenzie, has Asperger Syndrome. <br/><br/>I just set you on edge, didn’t I? You’re having flashbacks to <i>Real</i>, aren’t you? <br/><br/>Go ahead and release that breath you didn’t realize you’d been holding, because I’m here to tell you that this aspect of the novel is handled very well. <br/><br/>Ian hyper focuses on objects, he’s obsessed with patterns, he </span>
  <span id="freeText13121676186899418438" style="display:none"><b>2.5 stars</b><br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I’m rounding up to prove that I’m not a complete asshole all the time. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />So, first things first. The male lead in this book, Lord Ian MacKenzie, has Asperger Syndrome. <br /><br />I just set you on edge, didn’t I? You’re having flashbacks to <i>Real</i>, aren’t you? <br /><br />Go ahead and release that breath you didn’t realize you’d been holding, because I’m here to tell you that this aspect of the novel is handled very well. <br /><br />Ian hyper focuses on objects, he’s obsessed with patterns, he doesn’t always like to be touched, he has issues with eye contact, and he struggles to follow conversations if more than one person is involved. And this just skims the surface of the way his autism manifests throughout this novel. <br /><br />His quirks are at times endearing, at times confusing, and at times frustrating, for both the reader and the cast of characters surrounding him. And they’re meant to be, which is wonderful.<br /><br />You can tell that Ashley really did her research here, and I applaud that.<br /><br />What I found to be incredibly disappointing is that beneath those quirks, Ian is the same old tired, overused male lead I’ve found in so many other historical romances. <br /><br />I started to dread this being the case the moment he met the female lead, Beth, whose name I just had to look up even though I literally finished this book five minutes ago (that should tell you something, more to come on her later). <br /><br />So he meets Beth at an opera house. He knows her fiancé. He knows her fiancé is a huge tool. And he came ready to warn her away from him, with a detailed note detailing the man’s dalliances and perversions. <br /><br />Whether or not he gives the note to Beth is entirely dependent on whether or not he deems her worthy: <br /><br /><i>“I wrote it before I came tonight, in case when I met you I thought you’d be worth saving.”</i><br /><br />Seeing as how they didn’t even speak to each other before he slid her his missive, it’s safe to say her worth is based solely on her appearance. S’cuse me? Are you for real right now? Is that in any way supposed to endear him to me?<br /><br />WELL, IT DIDN’T. <br /><br />Then they actually speak, and during their first verbal interactions Ian began to covet Beth, to think of her as ‘his’. This mindset only became more pronounced as the book went on. I’m not sure if this was intentional or not, as a tie in to his autism, but his possessiveness of her, and her easy acceptance of it really bothered me because of how it was portrayed. It was domineering, dehumanizing, and objectifying. <br /><br /><i>“Tell Isabella’s gentlemen friends to keep far from you. I don’t want them touching you.” <br />“Only you can touch me?” <br />He nodded, brows together. “Yes.” <br />“I don’t think I mind that,” she said softly.</i><br /><br />I do. Cut that shit out. <br /><br />They refused, and Ian even goes so far as to force Beth into marrying him. This whole scene made me see red. Beth is a widow, not some blushing virgin terrified of her reputation being ruined. She’s very clear from the beginning that she only wants a physical relationship with Ian, and even turned down an earlier proposal from him. <br /><br />Then they get caught out during a liason by a douchebag cop named Fellows who has it out for the MacKenzies, and this happens: <br /><br /><i> “Ian turned around. “We are leaving by the front door. Be damned to Fellows.” <br />“I thought you said he was ready to arrest us.” <br />“Why should he?” Ian’s voice hardened, and he glanced at her with a look she didn’t understand. “He has no reason to arrest a man for spending a night in a pension with his wife.”<br />Beth stopped. “But I’m not your…”<br />She took in the priest, Mac’s expression, Curry’s innocently blank face.<br />“Oh, no,” she said, her heart sinking. “Oh, Ian, no.”</i><br /><br />Yuuuuuuuup. Yup. Yup. Yup. Silly, woman. This is the nineteenth century, what you want doesn't matter. Especially not to the one fucking person it should matter most to. <br /><br />Once they’re married, he continues to force his will upon her, even going so far as to use sex as a weapon when he doesn’t like the words coming out of her mouth: <br /><br /><i>“She bit her lip, white teeth on red, and his desire rose swiftly, inconveniently. But if he made love to her, if he rode her until she couldn’t breathe, she’d stop asking questions, she’d stop thinking, she’d stop looking at him.”</i><br /><br />Ew. That’s just…disturbing. <br /><br />Beth’s character is no better. She judges the females around her as gossip-mongering nitwits, and then goes on to relish in gossip with her friend, she betrays the male lead’s trust time and time again, and at the end of the book her TSTL tendencies drove me up the fucking wall. <br /><br />Then we have this little gem: <br /><br /><i>“This was the third day Beth had sat there studying the vista of Paris, the third day her paper had remained blank. She’d realized after her initial excitement of purchasing pencils, paper, and easel that she had no idea how to draw.”</i> <br /><br />That’s right. She’s so stupid she forgot she’d never had an art lesson before, never so much as attempted a sketch on her own. <br /><br />-______________________________-<br /><br />Lastly, there was the plot. It was not only predictable, but riddled with gaping holes wide enough to drive a carriage through, which I won’t get into because spoilers. <br /><br />In the end, the well-portrayed autism and the well-researched setting just weren’t enough to surmount this book’s many, many other issues. <br /><br /><b><a href="http://www.thealliterates.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thealliterates/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thealliterates" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/the_alliterates/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/thealliterates/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="13121676186899418438" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_47637976" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/47637976" />
    <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"><img alt=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1403239075p2/1570669.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/47637976?book_show_action=true">Feb 26, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"> Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of historical romance and beautiful love stories, unique characters</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=hero-in-pursuit">hero-in-pursuit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=less-than-perfect-hero-or-heroine">less-than-perfect-hero-or-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=heroine-i-adore">heroine-i-adore</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=hot-and-steamy-romance">hot-and-steamy-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=good-secondary-characters">good-secondary-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=abused">abused</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=hero-or-heroine-gravely-ill">hero-or-heroine-gravely-ill</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=family">family</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer47637976" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1184103738613611176">The Madness of Lord Ian Mackenzie established to me that it would be a great read from the first page. Ian is such an unusual hero, and he is thoroughly lovable. And Beth is one of those rare heroines who really does deserve a hero like Ian. Their relationship felt right and it felt meant to be. Watching them grow closer, to acknowledge their unique, rich relationship, was very gratifying. Their bond was emotional, sensual, spiritual, and intellectual. Although there were parts of each other tha</span>
  <span id="freeText1184103738613611176" style="display:none">The Madness of Lord Ian Mackenzie established to me that it would be a great read from the first page. Ian is such an unusual hero, and he is thoroughly lovable. And Beth is one of those rare heroines who really does deserve a hero like Ian. Their relationship felt right and it felt meant to be. Watching them grow closer, to acknowledge their unique, rich relationship, was very gratifying. Their bond was emotional, sensual, spiritual, and intellectual. Although there were parts of each other that they didn’t fully grasp, they kept their hearts open to coming to accept and understand each other. There were no judgments against each other given. Romance stories like this are my favorite kind: where two people can find love with each other, without judgments or the fear that they have to let go of who they are or lose who they are to be in a fulfilling relationship with each other.<br /><br />Ms. Ashley did a wonderful job of showing me who Ian was. That what others considered a ‘madness’, a defect, a shortcoming, was merely a different way of processing things, and very beautiful and worthwhile in its uniqueness. The depiction of Ian’s condition reminded me of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6869353.Water_Bound__Sisters_of_the_Heart___1_" title="Water Bound (Sisters of the Heart, #1) by Christine Feehan" rel="nofollow noopener">Water Bound</a> by Christine Feehan, another book that looks at a main character with a form of autism. It was not exactly the same as Ian’s, but I saw some commonalities in Ian and Rikki. They looked at the world in a profoundly different way, saw beauty with an enhanced detail that few of us are able to appreciate. Although that makes it hard to filter out sensations, the artist, the lover of beauty in me wonders how this can be a bad thing, if the person has the love and understanding, the space to breathe when things get too intense for them. Apparently Ian has <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asperger%27s_syndrome" rel="nofollow noopener">Asperger's Syndrome</a>. Back in the 19th century, no one would have known what this was, or understood it, and so for Ian to be able to function and to be productive, wonderfully so, was so lovely to read about. To see how his shame became a triumph. It was just beautiful to see. It really was. I loved the hope that Ms. Ashley gave me as I read. I know that she never tried to deny that Ian’s life wouldn’t be easy, but he had the love of his family, their acceptance, and the love of Beth to help him through it. So his affliction was really a gift. That is so true to life for us. Those of us who are different look at ourselves as flawed. However,I believe that our differences are God-given, and they are given to us for a reason. We may not see it that way, but as we walk through life, we come to realize that because of who we are we can give something special to the world that no one else can. That’s how I perceived Ian’s madness. Definitely a gift in disguise.<br /><br />I loved seeing Ian’s family. All big, tough, larger-than-life men, none of them perfect. They reminded me of my father’s family of brothers. A room full of big, loud-talking men. It made me smile. I am very much looking forward to reading stories about each and every one of them, and hopefully Ian’s nephew Daniel will get a book when he’s older too.<br /><br />This book was rich and fulfilling. I read it pretty quickly, because it fed my soul. I want to thank Ms. Ashley for giving us Ian and Beth’s beautiful love story.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1184103738613611176" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380403661ra/785330.gif" width="480" height="204" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>I am simply in love with this book!<br>I am in love with Ian! I am in love with Beth! I am in love with all Ian's brothers!<br>One of the most beautiful historical romances I've read! So magical!<br>Ian's "madness" made me love him even more!<br><br>I loved everything in this book! The story was amazing! The characters were AMAZING! The writing was simply beautiful!</b><br><br><b>BETH</b><br><br>I loved every thought that crossed her mind, everything she said, every move she made... everything! <br><br>She is not like some typical HR heroines and I think that is the reason why I loved her so much. She is not shy, she is not ashamed of her past, she is proud and will not allow anybody walk over her. The way she understands Ian, the way she makes him feel better, and the way she doesn't think of him crazy is just beautiful to read. She loved once and lost that love, and she is aware that Ian could break her heart, but she still wants to explore that desire she feels with him. I loved how she didn't let anybody walk over Ian too, even his brothers. I loved how protective she was even though she knew Ian could not love her back the way she wanted.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“It is the most divine thing imaginable,” she tried. <br>“I don’t want to hear about divinity. I want to hear about flesh and bone. Is love like desire?”<br>“Desire is part of it,” she said slowly. “The love for another’s body. But also love for their heart and their mind, and for all the silly things they do, no matter how absurd. Your world brightens when they walk into a room, dims when they leave it again. You want to be with the beloved so you can see him and touch him and hear his voice, but you want his happiness as well. It’s selfish, but not entirely so.”</i>
</blockquote><br><br><b>IAN<br><br>I was literally mesmerized with his mind! If this book was only his POV I would give it 10000 stars if I could! </b><br><br>The first time he saw Beth he just knew she was unique like his porcelain bowls, and he just had to have her. But not only for one night, he had to have her forever. So even though he always says he is not capable of love because of his "madness", I think he fell in love with her at first sight. She made him calm, she made him happy and she made him laugh, which he didn't do since he got back from asylum. He thought that everything he touches brakes and he only wanted to protect her from everything, even from himself. He never looked her in the eyes long enough because he would lost himself in them and he wanted to remember everything he did with her. He wanted her to belong to only him.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Right there in the damn box, with the opera blaring on. I’d take you, make you my own.” He put his hand on her neck over the spot where he’d given her the love bite. “I branded you.”<br> Beth smiled. “You, too.” She touched his neck. “I branded you.” <br>He laced his fingers hard through hers and pressed her hand to the bed. “Belong to me.” <br>“No one here to dispute that at the moment.” <br>“Always mine. Always, Beth.” Thrusts punctuated the words. Always."</i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380403661i/785331.jpg" width="448" height="276" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"He pulled her close. “Your being with me makes it stop. It’s like the Ming bowls—when I touch them and feel them, everything stops. Nothing matters. You are the same. That is why I brought you here, to keep you with me, where you can please make... everything... stop.”</i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380403661ra/785332.gif" width="498" height="208" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Because when I look at you, I forget everything. I lose all track of what I’m saying or doing. I can see only your eyes.” He laid his head on her pillow and rested his hand on her chest. “You have such beautiful eyes.”</i>
</blockquote><br><br><b>THE STORY </b><br><br>I am speechless! There is nothing I could say to give justice to this beautiful story! It captured my heart from the beginning! Even though I knew it had HEA, I just couldn't stop myself from crying near the end.<br>I think everybody needs to read this story, and needs to do it ASAP! <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Is this what love feels like?” he whispered to her. “I don’t like it, my Beth. It hurts too much.”</i>
</blockquote><br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380403661ra/785333.gif" width="500" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br></span>
  <a data-text-id="13380680392297641111" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_277556703" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/277556703" />
    <a title="Baba  " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4669232-baba"><img alt="Baba  " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1564910043p2/4669232.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/277556703?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Baba  " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Baba  " href="/user/show/4669232-baba">Baba  </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8204158-the-madness-of-lord-ian-mackenzie">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer277556703" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4636800273227017376">FULL REVIEW NOW POSTED<br/><br/>It's beautiful. It's thoughtful. It's special.<br/><br/><b>"Love you."<br/>The man who couldn't look anyone in the eyes was making himself do it, no matter what the pain. He was giving her a gift, the greatest one he could, straight from his heart.<br/><br/>4.5 stars.</b><br/><br/><i>London, 1881</i><br/>Ian had lived with a raw pain for so long. He doesn't always know how to express his emotions, but that doesn't mean he doesn't feel them deeply. Ian is a special man. He avoids to look people into their eyes and his attention</span>
  <span id="freeText4636800273227017376" style="display:none">FULL REVIEW NOW POSTED<br /><br />It's beautiful. It's thoughtful. It's special.<br /><br /><b>"Love you."<br />The man who couldn't look anyone in the eyes was making himself do it, no matter what the pain. He was giving her a gift, the greatest one he could, straight from his heart.<br /><br />4.5 stars.</b><br /><br /><i>London, 1881</i><br />Ian had lived with a raw pain for so long. He doesn't always know how to express his emotions, but that doesn't mean he doesn't feel them deeply. Ian is a special man. He avoids to look people into their eyes and his attention wanders when he is spoken to, and he interrupts conversations with inappropriate comments or questions that have nothing to do with the topic at hand. He can't follow a conversation when he's with a crowd. Further, he can't read hints from others. A person has to tell him a thing plainly. During Ian's stay at the asylum, he had to undergo a horrible "treatment". Obviously ice cold baths, beatings to suppress his rages, and electric shock "therapy" were common at that time. Since the electric shock therapy he suffers from terrible headaches on a regular basis. Ian was labelled as a madman, yet he is anything but mad. He's got incredible skills.<br /><br /><i>"I can play this piece note for note," Ian said, his breath warm in her ear. "But I cannot capture its soul."</i><br /><br />On top of that, Ian has outstanding maths skills and a terrific memory for certain things.<br /><br />It happens not all the time but for once I can say that I adored the heroine! Beth is kind-hearted, determined, stubborn, and she's got a will of steel. I think this woman can hold her own, and she did it all the time. She was Ian's constant source of strength and showed him a tremendous understanding. Beth is definitely <i>exquisite porcelain</i> and not a fake!<br /><br />On his trip to discover the true meaning of love, Ian has to struggle from time to time.<br /><br /><i>Explain to me what loving feels like, Beth. I want to understand."<br />"Desire is part of it," she said slowly. "The love for another's body. But also love for their heart and their mind, and for all the silly things they do, no matter how absurd. Your world brightens when they walk into a room, dims when they leave it again. You want to be with the beloved so you can see him and touch him and hear his voice, but you want his happiness as well. It's selfish, but not entirely so."<br />"I can feel desire and wanting. I find you beautiful, and I want you."<br /><br />"Is this what love feels like?" he whispered to her. "I don't like it, my Beth. It hurts too much."</i><br /><br />Ian is such a tortured soul and he did find his soulmate when he met Beth. This hunger and desire that both of them felt for each other was so palpable and ever-present. I was pondering about the word accessible. I guess autistics are difficult to access at times, yet I just felt that Ms. Ashley did a fine job in making Ian very accessible. I got an insight into his mind and I feel very grateful for that. We always have a need to voice everything. However, communication and understanding even work without a single word. Maybe we should listen more to our heart and our feelings. And facial expression and posture are other forms of communication. <br /><br />The Madness of Lord Ian Mackenzie is a beautifully written story. It's thoughtful, passionate and very sensual. The main protagonists are very likable and refreshing. Moreover, the author offers the reader a great cast of secondary characters as well. The story is nicely wrapped up by a lovely epilogue. I'm looking forward to reading the whole Highland Pleasures series!<br /><br />Ultimately, Beth claimed Ian's body <i>AND</i> soul and she helped him to control his "rage" and to deal with the misery that his deceased father did cause him.<br /><br /><i>"I'll make you sure. You said yourself he caused you too much misery and that you and your brothers need to be done with him. Please, Ian. Let him go."</i><br /><br />Ian did let him go and he said to Beth:<br /><br /><i>"I love you."</i><br /><br /><br /><b>On a personal note</b><br />Thank you, Kristen, for sharing your knowledge about autism and the link:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.autismspeaks.org/what-autism">http://www.autismspeaks.org/what-autism</a><br /><br />I appreciate it, and I truly hope that you will find <i>your</i> right and special moment to read this story</span>
  <a data-text-id="4636800273227017376" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_69472432" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/69472432" />
    <a title="Ridley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2543252-ridley"><img alt="Ridley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1251681007p2/2543252.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/69472432?book_show_action=true">Aug 30, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ridley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ridley" href="/user/show/2543252-ridley">Ridley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2543252-ridley?shelf=3-star">3-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2543252-ridley?shelf=read-2009">read-2009</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2543252-ridley?shelf=victorian">victorian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2543252-ridley?shelf=disabled-h-h">disabled-h-h</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2543252-ridley?shelf=paper">paper</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer69472432" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15725240766340930164">When I picked this book up knowing that it featured a hero with Asperger's, I imagined the crux of the story would be about Beth and Ian learning to love each other despite his emotional detatchment. I didn't feel like I got that.<br/><br/>There's no real discussion of how Ian and Beth came to love each other. I noticed they had great, wall-banging sex often, but that was the extent of the romance, it seems. There were few scenes that showed them interacting with their clothes on over something mundane. S</span>
  <span id="freeText15725240766340930164" style="display:none">When I picked this book up knowing that it featured a hero with Asperger's, I imagined the crux of the story would be about Beth and Ian learning to love each other despite his emotional detatchment. I didn't feel like I got that.<br /><br />There's no real discussion of how Ian and Beth came to love each other. I noticed they had great, wall-banging sex often, but that was the extent of the romance, it seems. There were few scenes that showed them interacting with their clothes on over something mundane. Sure, she supported him through a murder mystery, but how often will that come up in a lifelong marriage? I needed to see them becoming attached to each other and enjoying each other's company despite his communication quirks. I wanted to see them dealing with how utterly annoying an Aspie can be and how bewildering she could be through his eyes. Instead, he dominates her in typical alpha style and she accepts sex as attachment.<br /><br />Oh, and there's a murder mystery with a ton of plot holes.<br /><br />And a bunch of sex scenes thrown in for no particular reason other than to be graphic and to titillate.<br /><br />And a ton of obvious series set-up.<br /><br />Meh.<br /><br />Really, this is not the sort of character pairing that lends itself well to a suspense subplot (as half-baked as this one was) as there's plenty of conflict to mine from their personalities alone. I wanted a good book, a character study, and instead I got a paint-by-numbers romance novel like any other. It's not a bad book, just an exceedingly average one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15725240766340930164" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3079447110634931517">This is one of the best historical romances I have ever read! Beth is a widower, who inherited a small fortune after being a companion to a wealthy elderly woman. She's not exactly noble-rich, but enough that several men have come sniffing around trying to marry her. She catches the eye of Lord Ian Mackenzie, who people say is insane due to his strange public behavior, rages, and inability to act like everyone else in crowds. Ian has Asperger's, but is mainly the "high-functioning" sort. He is a</span>
  <span id="freeText3079447110634931517" style="display:none">This is one of the best historical romances I have ever read! Beth is a widower, who inherited a small fortune after being a companion to a wealthy elderly woman. She's not exactly noble-rich, but enough that several men have come sniffing around trying to marry her. She catches the eye of Lord Ian Mackenzie, who people say is insane due to his strange public behavior, rages, and inability to act like everyone else in crowds. Ian has Asperger's, but is mainly the "high-functioning" sort. He is a genius and can take care of himself, but has trouble making eye contact and understanding humor and emotion.<br /><br />Ian and Beth decide to have a liaison and, of course, it turns into true love. I loved Beth because she wasn't stuffy. She was kind and open-minded and a wonderful heroine. Ian was great too. There was very little angst, which I appreciate since I'm allergic to it. The drama was about a murder mystery instead of the typical separation and reuniting of couple.<br /><br />I just loved it from start to finish. I also really liked that it didn't take forever for the couple to get together. There were plenty of steamy scenes. <br /><br />I'm curious now to read about the other brothers!</span>
